This positions embodied action as primary teaching-vehicle. Contemporary embodied cognition research confirms understanding occurs through bodily engagement rather than abstract representation. Mirror neuron research reveals observing actions activates identical neural patterns as performing them, suggesting witnessing Sadāparibhūta's bowing triggers experiential understanding through neural mirroring rather than conceptual explanation. Teaching occurs through integrated gesture-speech act rather than information-transfer.

20. **Bodily Perfections as Karmic Fruit**: Following karma-exhaustion, Sadāparibhūta attains "purity of the eye faculty... ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind faculties," eventually acquiring the thirty-two major marks and eighty minor marks. This establishes karmic physics wherein mental cultivation produces somatic transformation. Recognizing Buddha-nature in others perfects one's own embodiment through karmic reciprocity—perceiving others as Buddhas generates karma whose fruit manifests as one's own Buddha-characteristics. This parallels mirror neuron research demonstrating mind-body bidirectional coupling: mental states produce physiological changes, and physiological configurations generate mental states. Buddhist soteriology positions the thirty-two marks as karmic fruits of specific mental cultivation. The chapter presents embodiment as karmic crystallization—body manifests as accumulated mental karma condensed into physical form. Sadāparibhūta's reverence-practice generates karma whose somatic expression produces perfected bodily marks.

21. **Six Perfected Senses as Culmination**: The chapter emphasizes Sadāparibhūta's attainment of "purity of the six faculties" (*ṣaḍāyatana*)—the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind senses achieving supernatural capacity. Buddhist physiology positions these as sense-bases whose purification enables direct dharma-perception. The text describes these purified faculties enabling extended lifespan, supernatural powers, and eloquent teaching—comprehensive transformation through single practice. Unlike Western domain-specific skill development, Buddhist cultivation assumes interdependent human systems wherein single-practice ripples throughout entire organism. Purifying one sense-faculty through reverence-practice necessarily purifies all because they share single consciousness-ground. This aligns with holistic development theory recognizing cognitive, emotional, physical, and social dimensions develop integratively. The chapter positions sense-purification as enlightenment-marker: Buddhahood consists not of transcending senses but perfecting them to perceive reality accurately. The six faculties become transparent to dharma—seeing actual forms rather than distorted projections.

22. **Medicine King Buddha Symbolism**: The chapter's implicit connection to Bodhisattva Medicine King (Bhaiṣajyarāja) from Chapter 23 establishes healing as primary dharma-metaphor. Buddhist soteriology fundamentally operates as therapeutic system: the Buddha as physician (bhiṣaj), dharma as medicine (bhaiṣajya), sangha as nurses, and sentient beings as patients suffering duḥkha. The Four Noble Truths mirror medical diagnosis: identifying symptom (suffering), determining cause (craving), confirming cure's possibility (cessation), prescribing treatment (Eightfold Path). Sadāparibhūta's practice functions as therapeutic intervention: reverence-bowing treats his own karmic disease (purifying offenses) and others' spiritual disease (planting enlightenment-seeds). The medicine-metaphor reframes salvation as healing rather than judgment—beings require treatment not punishment, cure not condemnation. This shifts theological framework from forensic (legal) to therapeutic (medical) soteriology: the problem isn't offense requiring propitiation but spiritual disease requiring treatment. The chapter positions Buddha-practice as universal medicine treating fundamental human disease: ignorance of one's Buddha-nature, cured through recognition-practice.

---

**Key References**:
- Buddha-nature universalism: Tathagatagarbha Sutras, Mahāparinirvāṇa Sutra
- Reverence practice: Bodhisattva precept texts, Mahayana vinaya
- Karma exhaustion: Abhidharmakosha 3.20-25

---

# Chapter 21: The Tathāgata's Supernatural Powers
## The Cosmic Demonstration of Dharma-Transmission
At that time, myriads of bodhisattvas—numbering like the dust-particles of entire world-realms—emerged from beneath the earth. These were bodhisattvas who had previously dwelt in the Sahā world. They approached the Buddha, bowed with their heads to his feet, and addressed him: "World-Honored One, after you enter final nirvāṇa, in the lands where your various emanations have taught and subsequently passed away, we shall extensively proclaim this Lotus Sutra. Why? Because we ourselves desire to obtain this true, pure, supreme dharma. We shall receive it, maintain it, read and recite it, explain it, and offer reverent worship to it[^1]."

At that moment, the Tathāgata revealed his great supernatural powers before all assembled—before myriads of old bodhisattvas dwelling in the Sahā world, before myriads of monks and nuns, before male and female lay followers, before gods, dragons, and all types of supernatural beings. The Buddha extended his broad, long tongue upward until it reached the Brahma heavens, and from every pore of his body, he emitted innumerable rays of light, illuminating all ten directions of the world-system. All the precious trees beneath which were seated the Buddhas from the ten directions, as well as Śākyamuni Buddha and the eternally present Buddha (Prabhūtaratna), similarly extended their broad, long tongues and emitted vast rays of light[^2]. The display of supernatural power continued for one hundred thousand years.

Afterward, the Buddha and all those Buddhas withdrew their tongues. At that moment, all the Buddhas produced a single sound of coughing and a simultaneous finger-snap. These two sounds echoed throughout the ten directions of all world-systems. In all those world-systems, the very earth underwent six kinds of trembling: trembling, quaking, roaring, cracking, heaving, and surging upward. Through the Buddha's supernatural power, all beings throughout the ten directions perceived this Sahā world-realm: they saw the endless precious trees beneath which the Buddhas sat, and they perceived Śākyamuni Buddha together with the eternally present Buddha, surrounded by infinite assemblies of bodhisattvas and the four categories of disciples—all offering reverent worship[^3].

All the celestial beings then proclaimed aloud in the void: "Beyond myriads of incalculable billion-billion world-systems, there exists a realm named Sahā. Within it dwells a Buddha called Śākyamuni, who now teaches all bodhisattvas a great Mahāyāna sutra named the Lotus Sutra, teaching the bodhisattva-path, guarded and protected by all the Buddhas. You should all generate profound reverence, offer sincere worship, and respectfully honor Śākyamuni Buddha!"

When those innumerable beings heard this proclamation, all brought their palms together toward the Sahā world. They offered varieties of flowers, fragrances, garlands, silk banners, jeweled canopies, and precious objects from the ten directions. All these offered substances rose through the air like clouds accumulating, transforming into precious canopies that covered the Buddhas of the ten directions[^4]. In this moment, the ten directions became unified and unobstructed, appearing as a single Buddha-realm.

At that time, the Buddha addressed the bodhisattva assembly led by Viśiṣṭa Bodhisattva: "The supernatural power of all the Buddhas is immeasurable, incalculable, boundless, and inconceivable. If I were to spend immeasurable, incalculable billions upon billions of eons explaining the supernatural powers, the merit, and the benefit of this sutra, I could never exhaust them. Therefore, in brief: all the dharmas possessed by the Tathāgata, all the sovereign powers of the Tathāgata, and all the profoundest secret treasures of the Tathāgata, all the exceedingly profound matters of the Tathāgata—all are revealed and proclaimed in this sutra. For this reason, after the Tathāgata's passing, you should receive, maintain, read, recite, explain, and write this sutra in all lands. In any land where this sutra is received and maintained—whether in a monastic garden, forest, tree-shade, monastic dwelling, or lay residence, whether in a hall or pavilion, in mountain valleys or wilderness—all such places should have stupas erected and offerings presented. Why? Because you should understand that all such places are bodhi-seats. It is in such places that all the Buddhas have attained unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment. It is in such places that all the Buddhas have turned the dharma-wheel. It is in such places that all the Buddhas have entered final nirvāṇa[^5]."
## The Cosmic Verification of Dharma
*At that time, the Tathāgata wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

All the Buddhas, saviors of the world,
Possess great supernatural powers,
Manifesting boundless miraculous deeds
To delight all sentient beings.

The tongue-faculty extends to the Brahma realms,
The body emits countless rays of light,
All to establish the bodhisattva path,
Revealing these extraordinary phenomena.

The sound of the Buddhas coughing,
And the sound of their finger-snapping,
Echo throughout the ten world-directions,
While the earth trembles with six kinds of motion.

Through the supernatural power of the Buddha,
All enable the maintenance of this sutra,
All the Buddhas rejoice together,
Revealing boundless supernatural powers[^6].

The merit and virtue of this person
Possesses no limits or boundary,
Like the endless space extending
In all ten directions without obstruction[^7].

Those who maintain this sutra
Have already seen me,
Have also perceived the Buddha Prabhūtaratna,
And all the emanation-Buddhas alike.

They have seen me in this present moment
Teaching the bodhisattva assembly.
Those who maintain this sutra
Enable me and my emanations,
Enable the eternally present Buddha,
All together to rejoice.

The Buddhas of the ten directions—
Both those of the present moment,
And those of the three times (past, present, future)—
All are seen and honored,
All receive offerings and attain joy[^8].

The Buddhas seated at the bodhi-tree,
The supreme secret dharma they obtained—
Those who maintain this sutra
Shall not long remain before obtaining them[^9].

Those who maintain this sutra
Possess inexhaustible eloquence
Regarding all dharma-meanings, terminology, and linguistic expressions,
Like wind moving through space with no obstruction.

After the Tathāgata's passing,
Know the sutra's meaning well,
Understand its causes and sequences,
And explain it according to the dharma.

Like the sun and moon illuminating
All darkness and obscurity,
Such a person walks through the world
Bringing light to all beings' darkness,

Teaching infinite bodhisattvas,
Establishing them in the one path (the Lotus teaching).

Therefore, those possessing wisdom,
Hearing of these merits,
After the Buddha's passing,
Should receive and maintain this sutra[^10].

Regarding the Buddha's path,
Without doubt or hesitation,
This person shall truly attain it[^11].

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 21 functions as a cosmic exclamation point, a demonstration that validates everything taught in the preceding chapters. The supernatural display—the extended tongue reaching Brahma realms, the light-rays illuminating all directions, the earth's six-fold trembling, the voice proclaiming across cosmos—are not mere theatrical effects. They constitute a metaphysical claim: that the dharma of the Lotus Sutra is verified by the entire Buddha-universe.

The extended tongue reaching the Brahma realms possesses profound symbolic significance. In Buddhist cosmology, the Brahma realms represent the highest reaches of conditional existence. The tongue—the organ of speech—extended to this limit suggests that dharma-transmission reaches the extremity of what can be expressed. Moreover, in Buddhist physiology, the tongue symbolizes the power of communication. A tongue extended to the heavens suggests that the sutra's words possess cosmic-spanning power.

The simultaneous display by Buddhas in all ten directions creates a mandala of verification. The historical Buddha Śākyamuni does not stand alone; he is surrounded and supported by all Buddhas across all space. Each Buddha from every direction performs the identical supernatural display, creating a unified, cosmic dharma-transmission. No Buddha differs from any other; all teach the identical sutra. This suggests that the Lotus Sutra represents not a particular teacher's innovation but the universal dharma of all Buddhas.

The six-fold earth trembling—trembling, quaking, roaring, cracking, heaving, and surging—represents a complete cosmic response to the dharma's revelation. Earth is not passive matter but a responsive being. The dharma's truth manifests physically, affecting the fundamental structure of reality. These tremors can be understood as the universe's acknowledgment of dharma-truth.

Most significantly, the chapter establishes that dharma-transmission is not limited to living Buddha-presence. The historical Buddha will pass away into final nirvāṇa. Yet the sutra itself becomes a continuing manifestation of Buddha-presence. Any location where the sutra is received and maintained—whether monastery or forest or lay residence—becomes a bodhi-seat, a place of enlightenment-attainment. This radical principle means that the Buddha's teaching function continues eternally through the sutra-text itself.

The instruction to erect stupas wherever the sutra is maintained reflects this principle at the architectural level. The stupa traditionally houses relics of the Buddha. But here, the text itself is declared to be Buddha-equivalent. The place where the sutra dwells becomes sacred space requiring stupa-honors. This suggests a sophisticated understanding that dharma is not merely abstract truth but concrete presence.

The cloud-like accumulation of offerings rising toward the heavens symbolizes the circulation of merit. The sutra's teaching generates merit that rises to support all the Buddhas; simultaneously, the Buddhas' blessings descend to support dharma-transmission. There is a continuous exchange between the Buddha-realm and the human realm, mediated by the sutra-text.

The declaration "the ten directions become unified and unobstructed, appearing as a single Buddha-realm" represents perhaps the sutra's most radical vision. Normally, the ten directions are separated by immeasurable distances; each Buddha-realm is isolated. Yet through the dharma-transmission of the Lotus Sutra, all realms merge into a single unified field. The boundaries separating Buddha-realms dissolve. This suggests that the sutra accomplishes not merely salvation of individual beings but the fundamental unification of all Buddha-realms, creating a cosmic sangha-body.

## SCHOLARLY APPARATUS

### Apparatus Summary

**Context**: Chapter 21 comes after the narrative exemplification of Never-Despiser and before the final assignment of the sutra's continuation. It functions as a cosmic demonstration validating all previous teachings.

**Central Teaching**: The Lotus Sutra is verified and authorized by all Buddhas throughout the cosmos. This verification takes the form of simultaneous supernatural displays that demonstrate the sutra's cosmic significance. The dharma-transmission is not individual practice but a Buddha-family activity spanning all of existence.

**Structural Function**: Chapter 21 elevates dharma-transmission from individual benefit (Chapters 17-20) to cosmic significance. It prepares for the final chapter's assignment of transmission-responsibility to the gathered assembly.

**Key Doctrinal Claims**:
- "All the Buddhas display supernatural powers to verify the Lotus Sutra"—establishes universal Buddha-authorization
- "Anywhere the sutra is maintained becomes a bodhi-seat"—elevates the text to sacred status
- "The ten directions become a unified Buddha-realm through the sutra"—claims cosmic unification through dharma
- "The sutra-maintenance continues Buddha-activity after the Buddha's passing"—establishes eternal dharma-transmission

**Philosophical Connections**:
- **Buddha-field**: The chapter's vision of the ten directions unifying into a single realm reflects the Mahāyāna conception of Buddha-lands as expressions of Buddha-consciousness
- **Dharma-body** (Dharmakāya): The principle that the sutra itself becomes Buddha-manifestation reflects the doctrine that the Buddha's ultimate body is dharma itself
- **Cosmic Buddha-network**: The simultaneous display by Buddhas in all directions suggests that all Buddhas constitute a unified body, all teaching identical dharma

#### Footnotes

1. **The earth-emerged bodhisattvas' vow**: These are the same bodhisattvas who emerged in Chapter 15. Now, after the revelation of the Buddha's eternal lifespan and the enumeration of benefits, they formalize their commitment to dharma-transmission.

2. **The extended tongue motif**: The extended tongue reaching to Brahma realms appears in other Mahayana sutras as a sign of Buddha-truthfulness. A Buddha's tongue can cover their face; when extended, it indicates extreme emphasis on the truth being spoken.

3. **The six-fold earth trembling**: This terminology appears throughout Buddhist sutras as a sign of great dharmic events. The six types of trembling—trembling (kampa), quaking (kampana), roaring (asvana), cracking (bhijjana), heaving (utthapana), and surging (uddhuvaṇa)—represent a complete cosmic response.

4. **Cloud-like accumulation of offerings**: The metaphor of clouds accumulating suggests that offerings multiply and concentrate. This reflects the principle that merit increases through collective participation.

5. **The three Buddha-functions at bodhi-seats**: The text specifies that at any place where the sutra is maintained: (1) Buddhas attain enlightenment, (2) Buddhas turn the dharma-wheel, (3) Buddhas enter final nirvāṇa. These three events constitute the complete Buddha-life. The implication is that wherever the sutra is maintained, all three Buddha-functions occur.

6. **Coughing and finger-snapping as sounds**: These seemingly casual sounds—a cough and a snap—become cosmic proclamations. The Lotus Sutra often uses ordinary human actions to carry ultimate significance.

7. **Merit as boundless space**: The comparison of merit to space suggests infinite expandability. Merit does not get depleted through distribution but rather increases through sharing.

8. **Three-times Buddhas**: The reference to past, present, and future Buddhas suggests that dharma-transmission spans all time. Every Buddha, whenever they exist, participates in this transmission.

9. **"Shall not long remain"**: This phrase suggests that enlightenment approaches swiftly for sutra-maintainers. The condition for Buddhahood is created immediately through the sutra-engagement.

10. **Inexhaustible eloquence**: The principle of pratibhana (inexhaustible dharma-speech) reappears here, suggesting that the sutra-maintainer can discourse endlessly on dharma-meanings.

11. **Without doubt or hesitation**: The final emphasis on certainty regarding the Buddha-path reinforces the sutra's central claim that enlightenment is guaranteed for all who maintain the sutra.

---

**Key References**:
- Extended tongue symbolism: Sukhāvatīvyūha Sutras, Tathāgatagarbha tradition
- Bodhi-seat (bodhimaṇḍa): Buddhavamsa, Mahayana Abhidharma texts
- Six-fold earth trembling: Throughout Pali Canon and Mahayana sutras

---

# Chapter 22: Entrustment
## The Final Assignment of Dharma-Continuity
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha rose from his dharma-seat, revealed great supernatural powers, and with his right hand touched the heads of innumerable bodhisattvas, speaking these words: "Through countless, incalculable eons, I have cultivated and perfected the supreme dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment. Now I entrust this dharma to all of you. You should all unite in mind and widely proclaim this dharma, causing it to increase and flourish[^1]."

Thus did the Buddha touch the heads of the bodhisattva assembly three times, each time declaring: "Through countless, incalculable eons, I have cultivated and perfected the supreme dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment. Now I entrust this dharma to all of you. You should receive and maintain it, widely proclaim it in all realms, allowing all beings to hear it completely. Why? Because I possess great compassion, complete absence of stinginess or miserliness, and no fear whatsoever. I am able to bestow upon all sentient beings the Buddha's wisdom, the Tathāgata's wisdom, and the spontaneously arising wisdom[^2]. All the Tathāgatas are great benefactors to all sentient beings. You too should follow the example of the Tathāgata, abandoning all stinginess. In the future age, when virtuous men and women who possess faith in the Tathāgata's wisdom approach you, you should widely expound this Lotus Sutra to them so that they may hear it fully. For what reason? In order that they might attain Buddha-wisdom[^3].

"Should any sentient beings not believe, not receive, and not maintain this sutra, then you should guide them through the remaining profound dharmas taught by the Tathāgata, demonstrating benefits to them through skillful teachings, giving joy and delight so that they gradually attain the bodhisattva path. All of you should thereby repay the graciousness of all the Tathāgatas[^4]."

At that moment, hearing the Buddha's instructions, all the bodhisattva assembly experienced profound joy that pervaded their entire being. Even greater reverence and respect arose within them. Bowing low with bent bodies, lowering their heads, and bringing their palms together, they collectively declared: "Just as the World-Honored One has instructed, we shall certainly fulfill this teaching completely. Please have no concern or anxiety, World-Honored One. We shall certainly receive and maintain, read and recite, widely proclaim, and explain this dharma in all lands, enabling all beings to hear it. We shall widely teach it, fulfilling the World-Honored One's instructions[^5]."

The bodhisattva assembly made this declaration three times: "Just as the World-Honored One has instructed, we shall certainly fulfill this teaching completely. Please have no concern, World-Honored One. We shall certainly comply with the World-Honored One's instructions, receiving, maintaining, reading, and reciting this dharma in all lands."

At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha caused all the emanation-Buddhas from the ten directions—Buddhas seated beneath precious trees throughout the universe—to return to their respective lands. The Buddha then declared: "Each of you Buddhas should rest content. The multi-jeweled stupa of the eternally present Buddha (Prabhūtaratna), may it return to its original condition." Hearing this instruction, all these things occurred as the Buddha proclaimed[^6].

At that time, Prabhūtaratna Buddha, together with Śākyamuni Buddha and all the emanation-Buddhas, the boundless company of bodhisattvas numbering like dust-particles, the leaders of the bodhisattva assembly (the Viśiṣṭa group), the śrāvaka assemblies of the four categories (monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen), and all beings throughout the world—gods, humans, asuras, and all—heard the Buddha's proclamation and all experienced great delight. Bowing respectfully with their heads to the Buddha's feet, they accepted his instruction as an eternal law[^7].
## The Eternal Transmission
*At that time, the Tathāgata wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

All the Buddhas, saviors of the world,
Dwelling in great supernatural power,
For the sake of the bodhisattva path,
Now entrust this dharma to you all.

My Buddha-dharma, accumulated across eons,
Through the cultivation of difficult practices,
Now I place within your hands—
Guard it and cause it to flourish[^8].

In all future worlds,
You should widely proclaim this teaching,
Never allowing it to be exhausted or lost,
So all beings may hear of it[^9].

Buddhas throughout the ten directions,
Both those present now and those of past and future,
Have all proclaimed through the gateway of skillful means,
But this sutra is supreme among all dharmas[^10].

Whoever receives and maintains this sutra,
Receives and maintains all the buddhas' dharmas;
Whoever reads and recites this sutra,
Reads and recites all the dharma spoken by all buddhas[^11].

Therefore practice with single-minded devotion,
Treat the sutra as the Buddha himself,
Just as you honor me with supreme respect,
So too honor this sutra without distinction.

In all places where this sutra dwells,
Whether in monasteries or in forests,
In gardens beneath trees or in dwellings,
Or in lecture-halls or any building—
In all such places should stupas be erected,
And all should make reverent offerings,
Gathering in masses like clouds,
Honoring this place as the Buddha's sacred site.

The Buddha, having attained enlightenment here,
Turns the dharma-wheel here,
Enters final nirvāṇa here—
All the Buddha-functions occur where the dharma dwells[^12].

After I enter the final extinction,
You should spread this sutra,
Causing all the world-systems
To hear of its teachings.

By this, you shall all repay
The kindness of the Tathāgata,
And quickly attain
Perfect enlightenment[^13].

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 22 completes the Lotus Sutra's structure with an act of formal transmission. The Buddha, about to enter final nirvāṇa, entrusts the sutra-dharma to the assembled bodhisattvas and beings. This creates a legal and spiritual bond: the assembly vows to continue transmission; the Buddha authorizes this continuation.

The threefold touching of the bodhisattvas' heads carries profound significance. This is a gesture of blessing and authorization, appearing in multiple Buddhist contexts. More specifically, it echoes the Buddha's original awakening at the bodhi-tree, where he touched the earth to witness his enlightenment. Here, the Buddha touches the bodhisattvas' heads to witness and authorize their dharma-transmission capacity.

The language of the assignment itself deserves careful attention. The Buddha does not give merely a teaching or instruction but assigns "the dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment" itself. This is not a verbal transfer but a trans-temporal event. The Buddha places within the bodhisattvas' "hands" (metaphorically) the actual enlightenment-dharma that took him countless eons to perfect. This suggests a radical Buddhist principle: that enlightenment is not a personal achievement but a cosmic dharma that passes from Buddha to bodhisattva to future-Buddha across eons.

The emphasis on "refusing none and fearing none" deserves attention. The Buddha declares that he possesses "complete absence of stinginess" and "no fear whatsoever." In Buddhism, stinginess (mātcharya) is listed as a fundamental obstacle to generosity and enlightenment. The Buddha's complete absence of stinginess means unlimited generosity—specifically, the unreserved gift of enlightenment-dharma to all beings. His fearlessness means that this gift is offered regardless of whether beings believe or reject it.

The principle that Buddhas possess three wisdoms—the Buddha's wisdom, the Tathāgata's wisdom, and spontaneously-arising wisdom—represents a sophisticated Buddhist epistemology. The first wisdom involves knowing all dharmas; the second involves knowing all beings' capacities and inclinations; the third involves spontaneous, effortless knowing that requires no deliberation. The bodhisattvas are authorized to transmit these wisdoms.

The provision for those who "do not believe, do not receive, do not maintain" the sutra deserves careful attention. The Buddha does not declare such beings forever lost. Rather, he instructs the bodhisattvas to guide them through "remaining profound dharmas" and "skillful teachings" appropriate to their capacity. This reflects the principle of upaya (skillful means): dharma-teachers adjust their teaching to each being's capacity, recognizing that the Lotus Sutra represents one of infinite dharma-gates through which all beings eventually approach enlightenment.

The response of the assembly—their declaration made three times—mirrors the Buddha's threefold transmission. This creates a symmetrical structure: the Buddha speaks three times assigning the dharma; the assembly responds three times vowing to maintain it. This parallelism suggests perfect understanding and alignment.

The geographical distribution of the emanation-Buddhas returning to their respective lands symbolizes that dharma-transmission is not spatially limited. Buddhas in all directions return to their realms, yet remain connected through the unified dharma-transmission of the Lotus Sutra. Distance becomes irrelevant; through the sutra, all Buddha-realms maintain continuous connection.

The reincorporation of Prabhūtaratna Buddha's stupa—returning to its "original condition"—suggests that the stupa's manifestation served a specific function (verifying the sutra through its presence) that is now completed. The stupa dematerializes or returns to its eternal form, suggesting that temporal manifestations serve temporary purposes while eternal dharma persists.

The final declaration that all beings—"gods, humans, asuras, and all"—accept the instruction "as an eternal law" is crucial. The transmission is not merely to bodhisattvas or humans but to all categories of beings. Moreover, they accept it "as eternal law," suggesting that dharma-transmission acquires cosmic legal status. It becomes not merely spiritual practice but ontological necessity, woven into the structure of existence itself.

## SCHOLARLY APPARATUS

### Apparatus Summary

**Context**: Chapter 22 concludes the Lotus Sutra's main teaching. It formalizes through ceremonial assignment what has been taught throughout the preceding chapters.

**Central Teaching**: The Buddha formally entrusts the dharma of unsurpassed enlightenment to all assembled beings, establishing their responsibility and capacity for continuing dharma-transmission after his passing. This transmission is not limited to a single era or location but extends eternally and universally.

**Structural Function**: Chapter 22 completes the sutra's movement from revelation (Chapters 1-2, where the Buddha announces the three vehicles will be unified), through demonstrations of universal Buddha-nature (Chapters 3-14), through the theological apex establishing eternal Buddha-presence (Chapters 15-16), through practical consequences (Chapters 17-20), through cosmic verification (Chapter 21), to final assignment (Chapter 22). The sutra's logical arc is complete.

**Key Doctrinal Claims**:
- "The Buddha entrusts to all beings the dharma of unsurpassed enlightenment"—establishes universal responsibility for dharma-transmission
- "Those who maintain the sutra maintain the Buddha himself"—identifies text with sacred presence
- "Wherever the sutra dwells, the Buddha's functions occur"—elevates the text to ongoing Buddha-manifestation
- "All beings, regardless of belief, receive skillful teaching"—reaffirms universal inclusivity
- "Dharma-transmission becomes eternal law"—establishes transmission as cosmic necessity

**Philosophical Connections**:
- **Three vehicles unified** (Chapter 2): The assignment to "all beings" completes the unification—all are now assigned the role of dharma-transmitter
- **Buddha-nature** (Chapters 8-9): All beings possess capacity to receive and transmit the dharma
- **Eternal Buddha** (Chapters 15-16): The Buddha remains eternally present through the sutra's transmission
- **Dharma-body** (implicit throughout): The sutra is Buddha's body; maintaining it is maintaining Buddha-presence

#### Footnotes

1. **Touching the heads**: This gesture appears throughout Buddhist rituals as a sign of blessing, authorization, and transmission. The threefold touching emphasizes the completeness and perfection of the transmission.

2. **Three wisdoms**: Buddha's wisdom (knowing all dharmas), Tathāgata's wisdom (knowing all beings' capacities), and spontaneously-arising wisdom (effortless, non-deliberative knowing) represent the three aspects of enlightened consciousness.

3. **The sole purpose: Buddha-wisdom**: The final clause "in order that they might attain Buddha-wisdom" reveals that every teaching, every transmission, every skillful means has a single ultimate purpose—the attainment of complete enlightenment.

4. **Guidance through remaining dharmas**: The principle that bodhisattvas guide non-believers through "remaining profound dharmas" reflects Buddhist understanding that the Lotus Sutra, while supreme, is not the only valid dharmic teaching. Different beings approach enlightenment through different gates.

5. **Three-fold vow**: The assembly's response, made three times, emphasizes the absolute commitment. This triple declaration creates a binding commitment, mirroring monastic vows that are typically taken three times.

6. **Return of emanation-Buddhas**: The emanation-Buddhas who gathered to verify the sutra now return to their respective lands, suggesting that the verification-function is complete and they resume their own Buddha-activity in their own realms.

7. **Eternal law status**: The phrase "accepted as eternal law" (śāśvata-niyama) suggests that dharma-transmission acquires cosmic legal status, not merely ethical status. It becomes part of the fundamental structure of reality.

8. **Eons of cultivation**: The verse emphasizes that enlightenment-dharma represents the fruition of countless eons of Buddha-cultivation. It is not arbitrarily given but represents the accumulated realization of Buddha-practice.

9. **Never exhausted or lost**: The vow that the dharma will "never be exhausted or lost" suggests eternal transmission. Unlike material goods that can be depleted, dharma-transmission is self-perpetuating.

10. **Skillful means as preparation**: The verse acknowledges that all buddhas of past and future teach through skillful means, but identifies the Lotus Sutra as "supreme among all dharmas." This establishes a hierarchy while acknowledging the legitimacy of other teachings.

11. **Identity of maintainer and recipient**: The principle that maintaining the sutra is equivalent to receiving all buddhas' dharma suggests a non-dual understanding where the maintainer and the dharma become inseparable.

12. **Three Buddha-functions at sutra-locations**: The enumeration—enlightenment, dharma-transmission, final nirvāṇa—represents the complete Buddha-life. Wherever the sutra dwells, all three Buddha-functions are eternally accessible.

13. **Quick attainment**: The final promise that bodhisattvas "quickly attain perfect enlightenment" through their commitment to dharma-transmission reflects the Lotus Sutra's most fundamental principle: engagement with this dharma swiftly leads to enlightenment.

---

**Key References**:
- Transmission ceremonies: Mahayana ordination rituals, Bodhisattva precept texts
- Three wisdoms: Abhidharmakosha and Yogacara texts
- Eternal law (niyama): Buddhist philosophy of natural/cosmic law

---

# Chapter 23: The Medicine King Bodhisattva's Original Practice
## The Bodhisattva's Extreme Offering
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha addressed the Bodhisattva Prabhūtaratna: "Inquire of me regarding the Medicine King Bodhisattva's original practice. How did this bodhisattva cultivate? What dharma does he teach? Pray tell us the history of this one we honor[^1]."

Buddha replied: "In ages past, beyond measurement in incalculable eons, there existed a Buddha named the Lord of Purity of the Sun and Moon—the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One, the One Perfectly Accomplished in Knowledge and Conduct, the Sugata, the Knower of the World, the Unsurpassable Guide, the Tamer of the Untamed, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. He possessed eighty billion great bodhisattvas and an assembly of seventy-two trillion enlightened śrāvakas. That Buddha's lifespan spanned four million billion nayuta eons. The true dharma remained in that realm for a period measured in years equal to the dust-particles of a continent. The semblance dharma likewise persisted through such measure.

"In that realm, there existed a bodhisattva named All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight—a bodhisattva who had long cultivated the roots of virtue, offered reverence to innumerable Buddhas, and perfected profound wisdom. This bodhisattva had achieved numerous samādhis: the samādhi of displaying all forms, the samādhi of dharma-blossoming, the samādhi of pure virtue, the samādhi of celestial play, and countless others[^2].

"At that time, the Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Lord taught the Dharma-Blossom Sutra to all sentient beings. All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight heard this teaching and, wishing to demonstrate his understanding, entered the samādhi of displaying all forms. From within this samādhi, he caused himself to manifest in an ocean of amrita (divine nectar) within the void itself. Having perceived one hundred thousand kinds of precious flowers blooming in that ocean, he declared: 'The dharma I now perceive through the Dharma-Blossom Sutra is so profound! I vow to honor the Buddha and this supreme teaching through ultimate offering.'

"Having made this vow, the bodhisattva collected all the flowers from the ocean of amrita and, gathering them together, presented them to Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Lord. The vast assembly received this offering and rejoiced greatly[^3].

"Afterward, the bodhisattva reflected: 'Though I have offered precious flowers, my heart is not yet satisfied. I now vow to offer my very body as a gift of honor to this Supreme Dharma Sutra.'

"The bodhisattva then gathered together all the celestial bodhisattvas, śrāvakas, and beings of the heavens, and spoke: 'All sentient beings, now listen! I vow to make an offering of my own body to the Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Lord and to the Dharma-Blossom Sutra!' Having spoken, the bodhisattva began an extreme practice. He ingested all manner of fragrant waters and precious oils—sandalwood, aloeswood, and other aromatics—for one thousand two hundred years. His body became saturated with these precious substances. Then, wrapping himself in silk and jeweled vestments, and anointing himself with expensive oils, the bodhisattva used supernatural power to ignite his own body as an eternal offering.

"His burning body radiated light across eighty billion nayuta realms. All the Buddhas in these realms perceived this offering and spoke these words simultaneously: 'Excellent! Excellent! This virtuous man has accomplished the supreme offering! To offer flowers, fragrances, garlands, or even entire kingdoms and beloved family members to the Buddha cannot equal this supreme gift of one's own body! This is the supreme offering among all offerings, the most exalted offering among all offerings, given in honor of the dharma and Buddha-realization. O virtuous man, through this supreme sacrifice of your body, you have completed the bodhisattva path!'

"After the bodhisattva's body burned for one thousand two hundred years and was finally consumed, he was reborn in that same Buddha-realm in the royal family. His consciousness re-emerged in his mother's womb. At that moment, the bodhisattva addressed his father in verse:

*'Great King, hear now my words—*
*I have wandered in that place,*
*And suddenly obtained the samādhi*
*That manifests all forms.*
*I have cultivated the supreme offering,*
*And I have burned my body,*
*For I seek the incomparable wisdom,*
*The wisdom of the perfectly enlightened Buddha.'*

"Having spoken this verse, the bodhisattva said to his father: 'The Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Lord remains present in that realm. I previously made offering to him and heard the Dharma-Blossom Sutra containing eight hundred trillion billion verses. Great King, I now vow to return to that Buddha's presence to honor him again.' With these words, the bodhisattva levitated into the void, ascending seven palm-trees' height, and approached the Buddha's presence where he again paid reverence and made offerings[^4].

"When this All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight Bodhisattva completed his remaining lifespan, he encountered two billion Buddhas, all called the Radiant Suns—Buddhas whose sunlight drove back all darkness—and in each Buddha's teaching he received, maintained, recited, and widely proclaimed the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. Because he taught this dharma to the four categories of disciples, his vision continuously clarified and he continued the practice of bodily offering.

"Subsequently, he encountered another two billion Buddhas, all called the Cloud-Kings-of-Radiant-Liberation, and similarly received their teaching of the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. Through his continued proclamation, he further perfected the vision-clarity.

"Having encountered countless billions of Buddhas, received the Dharma-Blossom Sutra from all, and proclaimed it widely to the four categories of disciples, his complete enlightenment-wisdom was perfected. He thus attained supreme, perfect enlightenment.

"Prabhūtaratna, do you comprehend the meaning of my account? This All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight Bodhisattva—he is none other than the Medicine King Bodhisattva who sits here before us! Such are the bodhisattva's past accomplishments. This Medicine King has offered his own body to countless billions of Buddhas, sacrificing his form as supreme homage to the dharma. This bodhisattva has completed practice across countless eons. These accomplishments are immeasurable[^5].

"Should a virtuous man or woman aspire to perfect enlightenment and yet offer only a single finger or a single toe in homage to the Buddha-stupa—such an offering exceeds all offerings of kingdoms, wives, children, and entire world-systems! Furthermore, if a virtuous person fills the entire three-thousand-great-thousand-world-system with the seven jewels and offers them to Buddhas, bodhisattvas, solitary-buddhas, and arhats—such an offering pales before the merit of simply receiving and maintaining even a single four-line verse of this Dharma-Blossom Sutra!"
## The Comparison of Offerings
*At that time, the Tathāgata wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

This dharma-blossom is supreme,
Most difficult to encounter,
Among all the teachings I have proclaimed,
It stands foremost.

Consider the four oceans with all their waters—
The ocean is foremost among all waters;
This Dharma-Blossom Sutra similarly
Stands foremost among all sutras[^6].

As the Sumeru mountain
Is highest among all mountains,
As the moon is supreme among celestial lights,
As the sun dispels all darkness—
So too this Dharma-Blossom Sutra
Shines most brilliantly among all dharmas.

A Cakravartin king rules all lesser kings,
Śakra rules the thirty-three heavens,
Brahma rules all sentient beings—
So this Dharma-Blossom Sutra is supreme,
The sovereign among all dharmas.

All śrāvakas and solitary-buddhas,
And all bodhisattvas bowing before this,
All those who receive and maintain this sutra
Are themselves supreme among the assembly.

Just as the Buddha is the sovereign of all dharmas,
So this sutra is the sovereign of all scriptures[^7].

This dharma can rescue all sentient beings,
Can liberate all from suffering,
Can provide complete satisfaction,
Like a cool and refreshing pool,
Like fire for the frozen,
Like clothing for the naked,
Like a merchant finding their captain,
Like a child finding its mother,
Like a traveler finding a ship,
Like the sick finding a physician,
Like the lost finding a lamp,
Like the poor finding treasure,
Like the people finding a king[^8].

Thus, if one hears this Dharma-Blossom,
And writes it or causes it to be written,
The merit-fruits are without boundary,
Cannot be measured by Buddha's wisdom itself[^9].

This sutra grants gifts most valuable:
To hear even one verse brings immeasurable merit,
To maintain it brings immeasurable reward,
To proclaim it brings immeasurable blessing[^10].

When Medicine King Bodhisattva heard this dharma,
He burned his own body as supreme offering—
Seventy-two thousand years the flames consumed his form,
That countless beings might perceive the teaching's truth.

After such offering,
When his body was entirely consumed,
He was reborn in that blessed realm,
Having sacrificed his flesh to honor dharma.

He encountered Suns-of-Radiant-Light—
Two billion Buddhas bore that name—
And in each Buddha's teaching he proclaimed,
The Dharma-Blossom Sutra widely.

Again he encountered Cloud-Kings-of-Liberation,
Another two billion Buddhas teaching dharma,
Proclaiming ceaselessly this supreme sutra,
Until wisdom's fruits were perfected[^11].

Having encountered countless billions of Buddhas,
Having proclaimed this dharma endlessly,
Having burned his body countless times,
He attained supreme enlightenment.

This Medicine King's extraordinary power
Comes from maintaining this sutra,
From burning his body in supreme offering,
From proclaiming dharma without ceasing.

If someone wishes enlightenment
And offers but a single finger
To the Buddha's stupa—
Such offering surpasses
The gift of entire world-systems,
The gift of precious kingdoms,
The gift of beloved family members[^12].

If one fills the cosmos with jewels,
The seven treasures in abundance,
And offers them to Buddhas
And bodhisattva assemblies,
This vast offering's merit
Cannot approach the simple act
Of receiving and maintaining
Even a single four-line verse
Of this supreme Dharma-Blossom Sutra!

Whoever receives this teaching,
Can expect rapid enlightenment,
Can anticipate Buddhahood's attainment,
Can look forward to dharma-sovereignty.

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 23 presents enlightenment-practice through its most extreme form: bodily self-immolation as dharma-offering. This raises profound questions about the nature of sacrifice, suffering, and the transformation of physical body into sacred presence.

The bodhisattva's practice unfolds in carefully structured stages. First comes the perception through samādhi (samadhi of displaying all forms). Second comes the flower-offering, which is subsequently recognized as insufficient. Third comes the ultimate sacrifice: the burning of one's own body sustained through aromatic-saturation for centuries.

The comparative logic is essential: even the most elaborate material offerings—kingdoms, treasures, family members—cannot equal the supreme offering of bodily self-immolation. This suggests a metaphysical claim that the body is ultimately the most valuable asset a being possesses. To surrender it is to surrender one's fundamental claim to existence.

Yet paradoxically, the chapter does not treat this sacrifice as termination but as transformation. The body burns for twelve hundred years yet consciousness is not destroyed. The bodhisattva is reborn immediately in that same realm, now embodied as a prince. What burns is not consciousness but form. The text presents this paradox without resolving it: the body can be simultaneously consumed and retained, destroyed and renewed.

The multiplication of Buddha-encounters is significant. This bodhisattva does not encounter one Buddha and achieve enlightenment. Rather, the pattern repeats across billions of Buddha-epochs. Each encounter involves the same practice: receiving the dharma-blossom sutra, proclaiming it, maintaining it. There is no final arrival, no termination of practice. Enlightenment emerges not from a single achievement but from eternal recurrence of the same fundamental practice.

The naming of this bodhisattva is itself instructive. "All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight" later becomes "Medicine King." The transformation from a name emphasizing visible form to one emphasizing healing suggests a spiritual development. The bodhisattva begins focused on perceptual transformation (all beings seeing) and ends focused on healing transformation (medicine-application).

The chapter also articulates a sophisticated economics of merit. Material offering, no matter how elaborate, produces merit limited by scarcity and finiteness. A person can give treasures and kingdoms because they are finite. But self-offering is infinite: the body's burning does not deplete the dharma; rather, each moment of burning constitutes a new offering. Time itself becomes the measure of gift-magnitude.

## SCHOLARLY APPARATUS

### Apparatus Summary

**Context**: Chapter 23 marks the transition from cosmic verification (Chapter 21) and eternal assignment (Chapter 22) to practical exemplification. It provides the first detailed narrative of a bodhisattva whose practice embodies the sutra's teachings.

**Central Teaching**: The ultimate dharma-offering is bodily self-immolation sustained across centuries, and this offering surpasses all material generosity. Through such extreme sacrifice, the bodhisattva perfects enlightenment across infinite Buddha-epochs.

**Key Doctrinal Claims**:
- "Bodily offering surpasses all material wealth"—establishes the hierarchy of offerings
- "Enlightenment emerges through repetitive dharma-proclamation across infinite Buddhas"—asserts eternal dharma-transmission pattern
- "The body burns but consciousness continues, reborn immediately"—demonstrates body-consciousness distinction
- "Medicine King represents countless Buddhas' teaching, not individual achievement"—emphasizes collective Buddha-activity

**Philosophical Connections**:
- **Sacrifice and transformation**: The bodhisattva's burning body represents complete sacrifice-transformation
- **Body-consciousness relationship**: The paradox of body-destruction and continuance raises questions about ontological status of form
- **Eternal dharma-transmission**: The pattern of Buddha-encounter-proclamation-reencounter suggests timeless dharma-circulation
- **Economics of merit**: Material offering has limits; dharma-offering multiplies through distribution

#### Footnotes

1. **Prabhūtaratna's role**: The eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna, who has been present since Chapter 11, is addressed as witness. This suggests that the revelation of bodhisattva-exemplars occurs under cosmic authentication.

2. **Samādhi enumeration**: The text lists bodhisattva-samādhis (meditative absorptions) that represent capacities: displaying forms, dharma-manifestation, purity, celestial play. These are not sequential steps but concurrent perfections.

3. **The amrita ocean**: The manifestation of a precious ocean within the void suggests that samādhi creates virtual realities equal in value to physical manifestations. The ocean's existence depends entirely on meditative perception.

4. **The levitation and verse**: The bodhisattva's spontaneous levitation and verse-declaration at rebirth demonstrates that enlightenment-consciousness maintains continuity across bodily death. The new body is immediately aware of previous existence.

5. **The past-present collapse**: The revelation that All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight is Medicine King collapses temporal distinction. The ancient bodhisattva is the present witness. Past and present are identity rather than sequence.

6. **Water hierarchy**: The comparative framework (oceans foremost among waters, mountains foremost among earthly features, etc.) creates a metaphysical taxonomy where each level has a supreme representative.

7. **Sovereignty metaphors**: The enumeration of sovereigns (Cakravartin, Śakra, Brahma) and the statement that the sutra is sovereign to all establishes a political metaphor for spiritual hierarchy.

8. **The list of comparable gifts**: The enumeration of gifts (water, fire, clothing, captain, mother, ship, physician, lamp, treasure, king) is poetic rather than logical. Each represents what a being lacks in specific conditions of suffering.

9. **Immeasurable merit declaration**: The repeated declaration that merit cannot be measured establishes that some goods exceed all quantification. Dharma-merit enters a different category entirely.

10. **Triple offering declaration**: The three forms of offering-fruit (hearing, maintaining, proclaiming) suggest that the sutra generates merit through all modes of engagement.

11. **Wisdom-fruit perfection**: The text specifies that "wisdom's fruits were perfected" only after billions of Buddha-epochs, suggesting that enlightenment is not a single event but a cumulative perfection across time.

12. **Finger-offering supremacy**: The principle that a single finger offered to a stupa surpasses kingdoms explicitly inverts material economics. Sacred offering operates according to different value-scales than material goods.

---

**Key References**:
- Bodily offering in Buddhist context: Jātaka tales, stories of bodhisattva sacrifice
- Samādhi practice: Abhidharmakosha, meditation manuals
- Comparative merit calculation: Larger Sukhāvatī Sutra

---

# Chapter 24: The Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva
## The Interdimensional Visitor
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha emitted the light-marks of universal brilliance from between his eyebrows, illuminating to the east one hundred eight hundred million nayuta realms. Beyond that number of worlds, there existed a realm named Pure-Light-Adorned. In that realm dwelt a Buddha named Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom-Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One, the One Perfectly Accomplished in Knowledge and Conduct, the Sugata, the Knower of the World, the Unsurpassable Guide, the Tamer of the Untamed, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. He was surrounded and honored by innumerable and incalculable assemblies of great bodhisattvas as he expounded the dharma[^1].

At that time, the light from the Buddha's eyebrow-mark illuminated the Pure-Light-Adorned realm, causing that Buddha and his assembly to perceive Śākyamuni Buddha's dharma-transmission. Within that realm dwelt a bodhisattva named Wonderful-Sound, one who had long cultivated roots of virtue, paid reverence to countless billions of Buddhas, and achieved profound wisdom. This bodhisattva had perfected eighteen kinds of dharma-gates (meditative absorptions and capacities), including the Marvelous-Banner Samādhi, the Dharma-Blossom Samādhi, the Pure-Virtue Samādhi, the Celestial-Play Samādhi, the Boundless Samādhi, the Wisdom-Seal Samādhi, the Gate of Understanding-All-Beings'-Language, the Samādhi of Gathering All Merits, the Pure Samādhi, the Divine-Play-Through-Powers Samādhi, the Wisdom-Torch Samādhi, the Sovereign-Adornment Samādhi, the Pure-Illumination Samādhi, the Treasury-of-Purity Samādhi, the Unshared Samādhi, the Solar-Revolution Samādhi, and countless billions of other dharma-gates[^2].

When the Buddha's light illuminated this bodhisattva's body, Wonderful-Sound immediately addressed his Buddha, Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom: "World-Honored One, I perceive that the light from Śākyamuni Buddha's form reaches here. I wish to journey to the Sahā world-realm, to pay reverence to, to draw near to, to offer worship to Śākyamuni Buddha, and to see Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince and other bodhisattvas, including Medicine King and Courageous-Giver. I also wish to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra[^3]."

His Buddha, Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom, replied: "My child, do not regard the Sahā realm with disdain or contempt. Why? Because the Sahā world is rocky and uneven, filled with dirt and soil. The body of Śākyamuni Buddha is diminutive, and the bodhisattvas too are small in stature. Yet your body measures forty-two thousand yojanas, while my body measures six hundred eighty thousand yojanas. Your form is supremely beautiful, adorned with hundreds of thousands of blessings and resplendent light, incomparably magnificent. When you travel there, do not regard that realm or its Buddha and bodhisattvas with contempt[^4]."

Wonderful-Sound replied to his Buddha: "World-Honored One, my journey to the Sahā world is entirely the power of the Tathāgata. It is the Tathāgata's miraculous display, the Tathāgata's virtue and wisdom adorning all things[^5]."

Having said this, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva did not rise from his seat, his body remained unmoved, yet through the power of samādhi, he manifested in the Sahā realm at Vulture Peak Mountain. Before the Buddha's dharma-seat, he created eighty-four thousand jeweled lotus flowers: their stems were made of refined gold, their leaves of white silver, their pistils of vajra-stone, their calyxes of precious carnelian-ruby stone[^6].

At that time, Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince, observing these lotus flowers, addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what is the cause and significance of this miraculous manifestation? What auspicious sign do these countless thousands of lotus flowers, with stems of refined gold, leaves of silver, pistils of vajra, and calyxes of precious stones, portend[^7]?"

Śākyamuni Buddha replied to Mañjuśrī: "The Great Bodhisattva Wonderful-Sound desires to come from the Pure-Light realm, together with eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas, to visit this Sahā world-realm, to pay reverence, to draw near, to offer worship to me, and to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra[^8]."

Mañjuśrī asked: "World-Honored One, what virtuous roots has this bodhisattva cultivated? What dharma has this bodhisattva practiced? What samādhi does this bodhisattva dwell in? I wish to understand the name of this samādhi, that we too might cultivate and practice it. If one cultivates this samādhi, one may behold this bodhisattva's magnificent form, the marks of his bearing and deportment. I pray that the World-Honored One will display his miraculous power so that this bodhisattva comes, and allow us all to perceive him[^9]."

The Buddha told Mañjuśrī: "The eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna shall display his form and reveal this bodhisattva's appearance[^10]."

At that moment, Prabhūtaratna Buddha addressed Wonderful-Sound from the jeweled stupa: "Come, virtuous man. The Dharma-Prince Mañjuśrī wishes to perceive your form[^8]."

Then Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva disappeared from the Pure-Light realm and, together with eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas, journeyed to the Sahā world. Wherever they passed, the six kinds of earth-trembling occurred, and the sky rained precious lotus flowers. Celestial music played spontaneously without being played. The Great Bodhisattva's eyes resembled vast blue lotus flowers. His face was exceedingly beautiful and dignified, surpassing the magnificence created by the merger of a hundred thousand billion moons. His body shone with the radiance of refined gold, adorned with hundreds of thousands of merits and virtues. His magnificence blazed with resplendent light; his marks and signs were all complete, as if embodying the steadfast nature of the mighty Nārāyaṇa[^11].

He ascended the jeweled platform, rose seven palm-trees high in the void, and approached Vulture Peak Mountain together with his bodhisattva-assembly. Upon arrival, he descended from the jeweled platform and, holding an ornament of pearls worth hundreds of thousands, approached Śākyamuni Buddha, bowed with his head to the Buddha's feet, and presented the ornament, speaking:

"World-Honored One, the Buddha Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom sends his regards. He inquires: Does the World-Honored One experience few ailments, few sufferings, and does he dwell in ease? Do the four elements remain in harmony? Is the world bearable? Are the people easy to teach? Do they experience little greed, anger, delusion, jealousy, and stinginess? Do they show respect to parents, honor monks, avoid perverse views and unwholesome thoughts, and guard their five senses well? Are the people able to overcome demonic armies? Has the eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna, who entered final extinction ages ago, come to listen to the dharma? And how is the eternally-present Buddha—is he peaceful, few-suffering, and able to remain permanently? World-Honored One, I wish to behold the eternally-present Buddha. Please reveal him so that I may see[^12]."

Śākyamuni Buddha said to Prabhūtaratna: "This Great Bodhisattva Wonderful-Sound wishes to meet you."

Prabhūtaratna replied to Wonderful-Sound: "Excellent, excellent, virtuous man! You have come to this realm to honor Śākyamuni Buddha, to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra, and to see Mañjuśrī and others. You have accomplished this well[^13]."

At that time, the Bodhisattva Dharma-Virtue asked the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what virtuous roots has this Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva cultivated? What dharmas does he practice to possess such miraculous power?"

The Buddha replied to Dharma-Virtue: "In ages past, there was a Buddha named Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Sovereign—the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One. In the dharma of that Buddha, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva cultivated celestial music as offering for twelve thousand years, presenting to that Buddha one hundred thousand varieties of musical instruments. Additionally, he offered eighty-four thousand seven-jeweled bowls. Through this karma, he was born in the Pure-Light-Adorned realm and acquired this miraculous power[^14].

"Dharma-Virtue, do you now see Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva sitting here before you? Though his body appears to dwell in this place, he simultaneously manifests in countless forms throughout the ten directions, teaching the Dharma-Blossom Sutra to all sentient beings. Sometimes he appears as a Brahma-king, sometimes as Śakra, sometimes as a self-mastering deity, sometimes as a great self-mastering deity, sometimes as a celestial general, sometimes as King Vaiśravaṇa, sometimes as a Cakravartin-king, sometimes as a smaller king, sometimes as a clan-leader, sometimes as a householder, sometimes as an official, sometimes as a Brahmin, sometimes as a monk or nun, sometimes as a male or female lay follower, sometimes as a wife of a householder or official, sometimes as a Brahmin woman, sometimes as a boy or girl, or even as a divine dragon, nāga, yakṣa, gandharva, asura, garuda, kinnara, mahoraga, human or non-human being. He manifests in these forms to teach the dharma. And he saves even those in the hell-realms, hungry ghost realms, animal realms, and the difficult-to-escape realms. He even appears in royal palaces as a female form to teach the dharma[^15]."

The Buddha continued: "Dharma-Virtue, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva performs such miraculous transformations and through wisdom illuminates the Sahā world, enabling all sentient beings to understand according to their capacities. Likewise, in the ten-directional worlds numbering like the sands of the Ganges River, he manifests in similar ways. Depending on whom he encounters: if a being requires the form of a śrāvaka to be taught, he manifests that form; if a solitary-buddha, he manifests that form; if a bodhisattva, he manifests that form; if a Buddha, he manifests the Buddha-form; if a being requires extinction to reach liberation, he demonstrates that extinction[^16]."

Dharma-Virtue Bodhisattva asked: "World-Honored One, this bodhisattva has cultivated such profound virtue. In what samādhi does he dwell such that he can manifest these transformations and benefit countless beings?"

The Buddha replied: "This samādhi is called 'Manifesting All Forms.' Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva dwells in this samādhi and thereby benefits countless sentient beings[^17]."

When the Dharma-Blossom Sutra regarding the Coming and Going of Wonderful-Sound was taught, the eighty-four thousand beings who had journeyed with Wonderful-Sound all obtained the Samādhi of Manifesting All Forms. Moreover, countless bodhisattvas throughout the Sahā world and the ten directions obtained this samādhi and dharma-gate[^8].

After paying reverence and offering to Śākyamuni Buddha and the stupa of the eternally-present Buddha, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva returned to his own realm together with the eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas. As they traveled through all the lands they passed, six-fold trembling occurred, precious lotus flowers rained, and hundreds of millions of kinds of celestial music played.

Having returned to his realm, Wonderful-Sound approached the Buddha Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom together with the eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas and addressed him: "World-Honored One, I have journeyed to the Sahā world and derived great benefit for all sentient beings. I have seen Śākyamuni Buddha, perceived the stupa of the eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna, and met Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince and other bodhisattvas including Medicine King and Courageous-Giver. I have also enabled these eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas to obtain the Samādhi of Manifesting All Forms. Moreover, through teaching this teaching of the Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva's Coming-and-Going, forty-two thousand celestial deities have obtained the recognition of the non-arising of dharmas, and the Bodhisattva Dharma-Virtue has obtained the Dharma-Blossom Samādhi[^19]."
## The Transformation-Manifestation
*At that time, the Buddha wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

From the eastern realm, beyond reckoning,
From the Pure-Light-Adorned World,
There came a bodhisattva named Wonderful-Sound,
Together with eighty-four thousand beings[^20].

He cultivated virtue in the ancient past,
And made celestial-music offerings
To the Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Sovereign,
For twelve thousand years continuously.

Through this offering, he attained realization,
And was born in that pure realm,
Where he dwells perfected in all merits,
In the light-adorned paradise.

He manifests infinite forms,
In all the worlds of the ten directions,
Teaching the dharma in countless ways,
Transforming according to each being's need[^21].

If one requires a Buddha-form for teaching,
He manifests as Buddha;
If one requires a bodhisattva-form,
He manifests accordingly.

If one requires extinction to reach peace,
He demonstrates that nirvāṇa;
In such boundless manifestations,
He performs his sacred work.

Upon hearing Śākyamuni Buddha's name,
And learning of the Dharma-Blossom Sutra,
He journeyed across incalculable worlds,
With eighty-four thousand attending companions.

Eighty-four thousand precious lotus flowers,
With golden stems and silver leaves,
Adorned with diamond pistils,
And ruby calyxes in profusion[^22].

The earth trembled with six-fold motion,
While precious flowers fell like rain,
And celestial music played spontaneously,
As the great assembly perceived his coming.

This bodhisattva's body measures vastly,
Forty-two thousand yojanas in extent,
Adorned with hundreds of thousands of marks,
Resplendent with wisdom and merit[^23].

The Buddha's eyebrow-light revealed him,
And all beheld the great being's form,
And heard the dharma he expounded,
The path of manifesting all forms.

All those who traveled with him,
Gained the samādhi of manifestation,
And forty-two thousand celestial deities,
Obtained the dharma-eye of recognition.

After paying reverence to the eternal Buddha,
And to the stupa of Prabhūtaratna,
The Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva returned,
To his own Pure-Light realm.

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 24 demonstrates a revolutionary principle: that bodhisattvas can exist in multiple Buddha-realms simultaneously and maintain autonomous agency even while being expressions of another being's miraculous power. The paradox is emphasized repeatedly: Wonderful-Sound "did not rise from his seat, his body remained unmoved, yet through the power of samādhi" he manifested elsewhere.

This suggests a Buddhist understanding of consciousness that is radically non-local. The bodhisattva's consciousness is not confined to a single body but can inhabit multiple manifestations without fragmentation. This is not reincarnation (sequential birth in different forms) but simultaneous manifestation (existing in multiple forms at once).

## SCHOLARLY APPARATUS

### Additional Analysis

The enumeration of transformation-forms represents the principle of upaya (skillful means) taken to its ultimate expression. The bodhisattva does not teach a single doctrine to all beings but adapts manifestation to each being's condition and capacity. Moreover, the forms themselves are doctrine: by appearing as a Buddha when Buddha-teaching is needed, or as a helper when help is needed, the bodhisattva's very presence teaches.

The interdimensional travel raises questions about the relationship between Buddha-realms. The chapter suggests that Buddha-realms, though distant, remain connected through the miraculous activity of realized beings. The light-ray that alerts Wonderful-Sound of Śākyamuni Buddha's teaching and his journey across dimensions suggest that the cosmos is unified by dharma-transmission even across seemingly separate worlds.

The relationship between the two Buddhas (Pure-Lotus-Celestial-Wisdom and Śākyamuni) is significant. The first Buddha does not hinder Wonderful-Sound's journey; indeed, both celebrate his coming. This suggests that Buddhas are not collaborative sovereigns but collaborative participants in a unified dharma-transmission spanning all realms.

### Apparatus Summary

**Context**: Chapter 24 continues the exemplar-narrative sequence begun in Chapter 23. While Chapter 23 focused on extreme bodily offering, Chapter 24 emphasizes unlimited manifestation-capacity.

**Central Teaching**: A bodhisattva who cultivates can manifest in all forms needed to teach all beings. This manifestation is not limited to a single realm or body but operates across infinite dimensions and simultaneous forms.

**Structural Function**: Chapter 24 establishes that Buddhahood (or advanced bodhisattvahood) includes the capacity for unlimited manifestation. This prepares for Chapter 25's focus on a specific manifestation form (Avalokiteśvara's compassionate responses).

**Key Doctrinal Claims**:
- "Bodhisattvas manifest through the power of samādhi while remaining in original location"—establishes non-local consciousness
- "Manifestation-forms adjust to each being's requirement"—applies upaya principle to embodiment itself
- "All Buddha-realms remain connected through dharma-transmission"—asserts cosmic unity
- "The samādhi of manifesting all forms is the key to universal teaching"—identifies specific meditation as prerequisite

#### Footnotes

1. **Light-mark revelation**: The Buddha's eyebrow-mark light illuminates to the east, suggesting that dimensional boundaries are permeable to enlightened activity.

2. **Eighteen samādhis**: The text enumerates eighteen dharma-gates representing different aspects of perfected consciousness: manifestation-capacity, dharma-mastery, purity, play, boundlessness, wisdom-seal, language-understanding, merit-gathering, purity, power-play, wisdom-illumination, sovereign-adornment, illumination, purity-treasury, unshared-nature, solar-revolution, and presumably others not enumerated.

3. **Cross-realm communication**: Wonderful-Sound immediately recognizes the distant Buddha's light and desires to visit, suggesting telepathic communication across dimensional boundaries.

4. **The warning against contempt**: The warning against despising the Sahā realm or its Buddha and bodhisattvas is significant—it reflects Buddhist understanding that all realms possess dignity regardless of their physical characteristics. Superiority of realm (beauty, size) does not correlate with spiritual importance.

5. **Attribution to Buddha-power**: Wonderful-Sound's statement that his coming is entirely the Buddha's power rather than his own effort suggests radical non-agency. Even the bodhisattva's manifestations are attributed to the Buddha's miraculous activity.

6. **Materiality as samādhi-manifestation**: The lotus flowers do not pre-exist but are created "through the power of samādhi." This suggests that material forms are emanations of consciousness-states.

7. **Mañjuśrī's role**: Mañjuśrī, the Dharma-Prince representing wisdom, consistently asks about teachings and their significance, functioning as the assembly's intellectual representative.

8. **Repeated emphasis on sutra-hearing**: Multiple characters desire to "hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra," suggesting that sutra-hearing is the central purpose of all dharma-transmission across all realms.

9. **Samādhi as prerequisite**: Mañjuśrī's request to learn the samādhi-name suggests that understanding the meditation-practice is prerequisite to perceiving the bodhisattva's form. Perception and meditation are linked.

10. **Prabhūtaratna as revealer**: The eternally-present Buddha is invoked to reveal Wonderful-Sound's appearance, suggesting that Prabhūtaratna's eternal presence enables inter-dimensional revelation.

11. **Nārāyaṇa reference**: The comparison to Nārāyaṇa (Viṣṇu) suggests that Wonderful-Sound's manifestation is so powerfully embodied that Hindu divine imagery is invoked.

12. **Elaborate courtesy and inquiry**: The formal greeting from Pure-Lotus includes elaborate inquiries about the Buddha's health, the condition of beings, and the state of the realm. This reflects Buddhist courtesy-protocol showing respect for a Buddha's authority.

13. **Prabhūtaratna's approval**: The eternally-present Buddha's acknowledgment of Wonderful-Sound's accomplishment shows that cross-realm actions receive cosmic authentication.

14. **Karmic causation**: The bodhisattva's gift of musical instruments in a past Buddha-realm directly produces the capacity for manifesting in the present. Gift-causation is explicitly stated as producing specific fruits.

15. **Manifestation-principle enumerated**: The detailed list of manifestation-forms establishes that upaya (skillful means) extends to form-manifestation itself. The bodhisattva's physical appearance is itself teaching-method.

16. **Extinction as teaching**: The principle that some beings require "extinction" (nirvāṇa-entry) to be liberated suggests that even final cessation can be a form of compassionate teaching.

17. **Samādhi-naming**: The samādhi is explicitly named "Manifesting-All-Forms," suggesting that Buddhist meditation has specific purposes and produces specific results.

18. **Collective enlightenment**: The eighty-four thousand companions all obtain the samādhi through proximity to Wonderful-Sound, suggesting that enlightenment can be transmitted through association.

19. **Multiple blessing-results**: The chapter concludes by enumerating multiple positive results: eighty-four thousand obtain samādhi, forty-two thousand heavenly deities obtain dharma-eye, Dharma-Virtue obtains the dharma-blossom samādhi.

20. **Interdimensional travel poetry**: The verse celebrates the journey across incalculable worlds, treating dimensional-crossing as ordinary dharma-activity.

21. **Manifestation-variety**: The verse emphasizes that manifestation adapts to beings' needs—Buddha-form for some, bodhisattva-form for others, cessation for still others.

22. **Poetic materiality**: The detailed description of the lotus flowers (golden stems, silver leaves, diamond pistils, ruby calyxes) emphasizes that samādhi-manifestations possess material beauty.

23. **Vastness and perfection**: The description of the bodhisattva's form emphasizes both vast scale (42,000 yojanas) and perfect adornment (hundreds of thousands of marks).

---

**Key References**:
- Manifestation-forms (nirmāṇakāya): Trikāya doctrine, Yogācāra philosophy
- Samādhi-practice results: Abhidharmakosha meditation sections
- Interdimensional contact: Vimalakirti Sutra, other Mahāyāna sutras

---

# Chapter 25: Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva's Gateway of Universal Access
## The Bodhisattva of Boundless Compassion
At that time, the Bodhisattva Boundless-Intention rose from his seat, bowed respectfully with his head to the Buddha's feet, and posed this inquiry: "World-Honored One, I wish to ask: For what reason is the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara called by this name[^1]?"

The Buddha replied: "Excellent question, Boundless-Intention. If countless billions of sentient beings experiencing suffering hear the name Avalokiteśvara and call upon this bodhisattva with sincere intention, the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara will immediately perceive the sound of their invocation. That being will at once gain liberation. For this reason, this bodhisattva is named Avalokiteśvara—the One Who Perceives the World's Sounds of Suffering[^2].

"If a being faces great fire and calls upon Avalokiteśvara, the flames cannot burn such a person, because the bodhisattva's power of wisdom prevents the fire from destroying them. If one is swept away by a great flood and cries out to Avalokiteśvara, one will suddenly find oneself in shallow water. If a hundred thousand billion sentient beings venture onto the great ocean seeking treasures—silver, lapis lazuli, crystal, agate, coral, amber, pearls and other jewels—and their boat is caught in a black wind and driven toward the realm of the rākṣasa demons, a single person among them calling upon Avalokiteśvara will rescue all from the danger of the demons[^3].

"If someone faces impending execution and invokes Avalokiteśvara, the executioner's weapons will shatter into fragments and the condemned person will escape. If a being is bound with chains or shackles and calls upon this bodhisattva, all restraints will break free, and that person will attain liberation. If a region is filled with countless night-demons and rākṣasas intending to cause harm, and they hear the name Avalokiteśvara invoked, these harmful beings will not dare even look upon the invocant with malice, much less cause injury[^4].

"Moreover, Boundless-Intention, if a being harbors excessive lust and constantly honors and reveres Avalokiteśvara, that being will be liberated from lust. If one is enslaved by anger, constant reverence to Avalokiteśvara brings liberation from anger. If one is trapped in delusion, such reverence brings freedom from delusion[^5].

"Avalokiteśvara possesses such great divine power. If one wishes to bear a son, one should reverence and offer to this bodhisattva, and one will birth a virtuous, wise, and meritorious son. If one wishes a daughter, one will birth a beautiful, accomplished, and virtuous daughter, beloved and respected by all.

"Boundless-Intention, any sentient being who venerates Avalokiteśvara will not lose the fruit of that reverence. For this reason, all beings should always turn their thoughts toward this bodhisattva.

"If someone sustains the names of sixty-two billion Bodhisattvas equal to the dust of the Ganges River, and provides them with all necessities—food, clothing, bedding, and medicine—throughout their lives, what merit would they accumulate?"

Boundless-Intention replied: "Immeasurable, World-Honored One."

The Buddha declared: "If another person sustains the name of Avalokiteśvara, even offering a single moment of reverence, the merit would be identical—no difference whatsoever. Even through incalculable billions of eons, the merit could never be exhausted[^6].

"Boundless-Intention, if I were to teach all the dharmas concerning how Avalokiteśvara traverses this world, in what manner Avalokiteśvara teaches the dharma through skillful means, the discussion would require incalculable eons. Therefore, in summary: all sentient beings experiencing anxiety and distress, if they hear of Avalokiteśvara, will find immediate relief through the bodhisattva's power of wise compassion. For this reason, all should trust in Avalokiteśvara[^7]."
## The Thirty-Three Manifestations
